<div id="review_3020622576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3020622576" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44185854-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435618493p2/44185854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3020622576?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/44185854-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44185854-jane?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44185854-jane?shelf=award-winners">award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44185854-jane?shelf=newbery-books">newbery-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44185854-jane?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3020622576&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3020622576" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10460800404191315107">This book was not what I expected and I loved that.<br/><br/>Set in the western front of the US Civil War, Rifles for Watie is a fascinating look at a single soldier (Jefferson Davis Bussey) and his experiences on the war front. <br/><br/>Things I enjoyed/was fascinated by:<br/>*Varying reasons for going to war. In school, we learn that everyone was at war because of slavery but it was so much more complex than that. Bushwhackers where terrorizing people that thought differently then them--stealing, hurting, and even ki</span>
  <span id="freeText10460800404191315107" style="display:none">This book was not what I expected and I loved that.<br /><br />Set in the western front of the US Civil War, Rifles for Watie is a fascinating look at a single soldier (Jefferson Davis Bussey) and his experiences on the war front. <br /><br />Things I enjoyed/was fascinated by:<br />*Varying reasons for going to war. In school, we learn that everyone was at war because of slavery but it was so much more complex than that. Bushwhackers where terrorizing people that thought differently then them--stealing, hurting, and even killing others. Then people want freedom of choice and their land and to keep their families safe. <br />*Contrast between life in teh Union camps versus the Confederate camps. So interesting to see how well Jeff is treated when he is sick behind enemy lines and the relationships he builds there<br />*Jeff's romance with Lucy. I love the evolution of their relationship and the way they respect each other and their passions and reasons for going to war. Really mature overall.<br />*Day to day life as a union soldier and the realities of battle. I really haven't read much about this time period and was fascinated by the young soldier and his excitement for battle. Then his disappointment as he must wait to actually experience something that isn't what he expects. Interesting to see solider interactions, shortages of supplies, raiding for food nearby, how quickly things change and how unexpected death is even in a war.<br />*Jeff's progression as a character. He is so innocent and looking forward to the glory of war at the start, and then he experiences loss, hunger, fatigue, false accusations, and even spying. He develops relationships with people on both sides of the fight. And they change him. But through it all, he remains a loyal, hard working, good person. And I admired him.<br /><br />A few qualms:<br />*The summary on the cover of my library copy of the book was misleading. I thought Jeff would be spying a lot sooner on the confederates. That's not until at least 2/3rds thru the book. The anticipation was a bit distracting at times.<br />*How can Claucey get away with so much murder and intrigue before finally being brought to justice?!<br />*Jeff's final race to the fort when he is nearly caught, starved to death and collapses of fatigue is intense. And I just wonder how realistic. The dog just decides to be his friend? It was a bit silly closure to a very intense set of scenes. Of course, I'm glad he survived and is able to help the Union but I didn't love that twist.<br /><br />Overall, a fascinating novel. Well deserved Newbery with compelling themes and complex characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10460800404191315107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2506367593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2506367593" />
    <a title="Phoebe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2807810-phoebe"><img alt="Phoebe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596327344p2/2807810.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2506367593?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phoebe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phoebe" href="/user/show/2807810-phoebe">Phoebe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807810-phoebe?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807810-phoebe?shelf=civil-war">civil-war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807810-phoebe?shelf=historical-19th-century">historical-19th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2807810-phoebe?shelf=1860s">1860s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2506367593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13187746448212859347">Newbery books are a special breed, and this oldie-but-goodie rings true. Beautiful writing that nonetheless is accessible and down to earth enough for junior high readers carries an exciting story of the Civil War seen through the eyes of a 16 year old Kansas boy. Jeff Bussey is an appealing protagonist, a courageous, sensible teenage boy eager to join the Union efforts and gain battle experience. He has no idea what unusual paths his life will take over the next four years. This makes quite a t</span>
  <span id="freeText13187746448212859347" style="display:none">Newbery books are a special breed, and this oldie-but-goodie rings true. Beautiful writing that nonetheless is accessible and down to earth enough for junior high readers carries an exciting story of the Civil War seen through the eyes of a 16 year old Kansas boy. Jeff Bussey is an appealing protagonist, a courageous, sensible teenage boy eager to join the Union efforts and gain battle experience. He has no idea what unusual paths his life will take over the next four years. This makes quite a tale. Keith focuses on the Civil War battles in the Western part of the country and the Cherokee Confederate Indian Cavalry general, Stand Watie. The Native Americans who fought on the Confederate side often owned slaves, and they were also fighting for the preservation of prosperous lifestyles: large houses, fertile farms and plantations, wealth and dignity. While this book is just a plain good read, it is also important, covering obscure elements of the Civil War and really conveying for young readers how blurry war can be, as we feel Jeff's conflict as he gets to know the enemy but ultimately remembers why the Union must win. This novel deserves its Newbery status. Published in 1957, it does use the word Negro. Otherwise, the writing feels surprisingly current. Junior high, up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13187746448212859347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2993705559889440327">I liked this much more than I would have expected to. I'm not a history buff and don't have much interest in American history, but once I got all the terminology straight I was hooked. Keith's portrayal of war and death are dark and meaningful without being "too much" for older children. Jeff is a great character and his coming-of-age progression is complex and well done. I loved his integrity and his understanding and sympathy for both sides by the end of the novel. And the last 50 or so pages </span>
  <span id="freeText2993705559889440327" style="display:none">I liked this much more than I would have expected to. I'm not a history buff and don't have much interest in American history, but once I got all the terminology straight I was hooked. Keith's portrayal of war and death are dark and meaningful without being "too much" for older children. Jeff is a great character and his coming-of-age progression is complex and well done. I loved his integrity and his understanding and sympathy for both sides by the end of the novel. And the last 50 or so pages are absolutely thrilling.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uzns+69JwbDXaOx4/Dlfb6fvU/7gAIBBjXxkshulEVHvuei7QolQHbMslLQfTa1imZw0tpQ2yejoKSwGVNJFUQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/70750.Harold_Keith">About Harold Keith</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/70750.Harold_Keith"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1516245845p3/70750.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/70750.Harold_Keith">Harold Keith
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
11
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12525828491972165067"> Harold Keith lived his entire life in Oklahoma, a state that he greatly loved and which served as the setting for many of his books.<br/> Perhaps his best known story, the historical novel "Rifles for Watie", was first released in 1957. It went on to win the 1958 John Newbery Medal and the 1964 Lewis Carroll Shelf Award.<br/> In 1998, Harold Keith died of congestive heart failure, in Norman, Oklahoma. </span>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
